      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: IAUC90
      

      m. The mean intracellular water lifetime (i). Used in the Shutter-Speed
      Model (SSM) of tracer kinetics
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: Tau_m
      

      vp. The fractional (not absolute) blood plasma volume per unit volume of
      tissue. See Tofts et al, "Estimating Kinetic Parameters From Dynamic Contrast-
      Enhanced T1-Weighted MRI of a Diffusable Tracer: Standardized Quantities and
      Symbols", Journal of Magnetic Resonance Imaging, vol. 10, pp. 223-232, 1999
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: Vp
      

      A tracer diffusion kinetic model in which the permeability is assumed to be
      isodirectional. See P. Tofts, "Modeling tracer kinetics in dynamic Gd-DTPA MR
      imaging", Journal of Magnetic Resonance Imaging, vol. 7, pp. 91-101, 1997
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: StandardToftsModel
      

      A tracer diffusion kinetic model in which the permeability is not assumed to
      be isodirectional, and which includes the contribution of tracer in the blood
      plasma to the total tissue concentration. See P. Tofts, "Modeling tracer
      kinetics in dynamic Gd-DTPA MR imaging", Journal of Magnetic Resonance
      Imaging, vol. 7, pp. 91-101, 1997
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: ExtendedToftsModel
      

      A semiquantitative analysis of the contrast-enhancement concentration versus
      time curve that avoids the use of a pharmacokinetic model; e.g. integration to
      compute the initial area under the curve
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: Model_freeConcentration_timeQuantitification
      

      A tracer diffusion kinetic model that accounts for the tumor leakage profile
      during the first pass of contrast. See Li, Ka-Loh, Xiao Ping Zhu, John
      Waterton, and Alan Jackson. "Improved 3D Quantitative Mapping of Blood Volume
      and Endothelial Permeability in Brain Tumors." Journal of Magnetic Resonance
      Imaging 12, no. 2 (2000): 347-357. doi:10.1002/1522-2586(200008)12:2<347::AID-
      JMRI19>3.0.CO;2-7
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: FirstPassLeakageProfile_FPLP_
      

      A tracer diffusion kinetic model that does not assume that intercompartmental
      water molecule exchange is infinitely fast. See Li, Xin, Wei Huang, Thomas E.
      Yankeelov, Alina Tudorica, William D. Rooney, and Charles S. Springer.
      "Shutter-Speed Analysis of Contrast Reagent Bolus-Tracking Data: Preliminary
      Observations in Benign and Malignant Breast Disease." Magnetic Resonance in
      Medicine 53, no. 3 (2005): 724-29. doi:10.1002/mrm.20405
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: Shutter_SpeedModel_SSM_
      

      T1 measurement by Multiple Flip Angles (MFA) (variable saturation) method
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: T1ByMultipleFlipAngles
      

      T1 measurement by Inversion Recovery (IR) method
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: T1ByInversionRecovery
      

      Calculation was performed using a fixed value of T1 rather than a measured
      value. The value could be encoded as the value of (126353, DCM, "T1 Used For
      Calculation")
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: T1ByFixedValue
      

      The fixed value of T1 used for a calculation
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: T1UsedForCalculation
      

      No Arterial Input Function was used
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: AIFIgnored
      

      A population-averaged Arterial Input Function
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: PopulationAveragedAIF
      

      An Arterial Input Function computed from a user-defined Region of Interest
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: User_definedAIFROI
      

      An Arterial Input Function computed from an automatically detected Region of
      Interest
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: AutomaticallyDetectedAIFROI
      

      A data-driven blind source separation (BSS) algorithm that estimates AIF from
      individuals without any presumed AIF model and initialization. See Lin, Yu-
      Chun, Tsung-Han Chan, Chong-Yung Chi, Shu-Hang Ng, Hao-Li Liu, Kuo-Chen Wei,
      Yau-Yau Wai, Chun-Chieh Wang, and Jiun-Jie Wang. "Blind Estimation of the
      Arterial Input Function in Dynamic Contrast-Enhanced MRI Using Purity
      Maximization." Magnetic Resonance in Medicine 68, no. 5 (November 1, 2012):
      1439-49. doi:10.1002/mrm.24144
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: BlindEstimationOfAIF
      

      The time at which the concentration-time curve achieves its peak for the first
      time. Used as a concept name for a value or as a method; e.g. used as a method
      of calculation for BAT. See Shpilfoygel Med Phys 2008. doi: 10.1118/1.1288669
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: TimeOfPeakConcentration
      

      The nominal time at which arrival of a contrast bolus is detected, which is
      used as a reference point for subsequent calculations. Used as a concept name
      for a value or as a method. No specific computational method is implied by
      this general definition. Abbreviated BAT
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: BolusArrivalTime
      

      The time at which the concentration-time curve achieves half of its peak
      density for the first time. Used as a concept name for a value or as a method;
      e.g. used as a method of calculation for BAT. See Shpilfoygel Med Phys 2008.
      doi: 10.1118/1.1288669
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: TimeOfLeadingHalf_PeakConcentration
      

      A method of determining BAT that involves computing the temporal derivative of
      the concentration-time curve and selecting the time when the temporal
      derivative exceeds a specified threshold. See Shpilfoygel Med Phys 2008. doi:
      10.1118/1.1288669
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: TemporalDerivativeExceedsThreshold
      

      A threshold applied to the temporal derivative of the concentration-time
      curve; e.g. used to establish BAT. See Shpilfoygel Med Phys 2008. doi:
      10.1118/1.1288669
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: TemporalDerivativeThreshold
      

      The maximum rate of signal intensity change within a measured region of a
      time-activity curve. See Boonsirikamchai, Piyaporn, Harmeet Kaur, Deborah A.
      Kuban, Edward Jackson, Ping Hou, and Haesun Choi. "Use of Maximum Slope Images
      Generated From Dynamic Contrast-Enhanced MRI to Detect Locally Recurrent
      Prostate Carcinoma After Prostatectomy: A Practical Approach." American
      Journal of Roentgenology 198, no. 3 (March 1, 2012): W228-W236.
      doi:10.2214/AJR.10.6387
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: MaximumSlope
      

      The maximum degree of signal intensity change within a measured region of a
      time-activity curve. See Boonsirikamchai, Piyaporn, Harmeet Kaur, Deborah A.
      Kuban, Edward Jackson, Ping Hou, and Haesun Choi. "Use of Maximum Slope Images
      Generated From Dynamic Contrast-Enhanced MRI to Detect Locally Recurrent
      Prostate Carcinoma After Prostatectomy: A Practical Approach." American
      Journal of Roentgenology 198, no. 3 (March 1, 2012): W228-W236.
      doi:10.2214/AJR.10.6387
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: MaximumDifference
      

      Tracer concentration in tissue; e.g. in a DCE-MR experiment, the concentration
      of contrast agent in mmol/l
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: TracerConcentration
      

      The degree to which a paramagnetic contrast agent can enhance the proton
      longitudinal relaxation rate constant (R1, 1/T1), normalized to the
      concentration of the contrast agent. Also referred to as r1. Typically
      expressed in units of l/mmol/s
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: ContrastLongitudinalRelaxivity
      

      The flow rate of blood perfusing a region as volume per mass per unit of time
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: RegionalBloodFlow
      

      The volume of blood perfusing a region as volume per mass
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: RegionalBloodVolume
      

      The percent of the oxygen removed from the blood by tissue during its passage
      through the capillary network. For example, as measured by blood oxygenation
      level dependent (BOLD) MR. See He, Xiang, and Dmitriy A. Yablonskiy.
      "Quantitative BOLD: Mapping of Human Cerebral Deoxygenated Blood Volume and
      Oxygen Extraction Fraction: Default State." Magnetic Resonance in Medicine 57,
      no. 1 (2007): 115-26
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: OxygenExtractionFraction
      

      The longitiudinal relaxation rate constant. The inverse of longitudinal
      relaxation time, i.e., R1 = 1/T1
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: R1
      

      The transverse relaxation rate constant. The inverse of transverse relaxation
      time, i.e., R2 = 1/T2
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: R2
      

      A ratio of locally measured radioactivity concentration versus the injected
      radioactivity distributed evenly throughout the whole body. This general
      concept encompasses all specific methods of calculating the whole body volume
      of distribution, such as using body weight, lean body mass, body surface area,
      etc.
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: StandardizedUptakeValue
      

      Standardized Uptake Value calculated using body weight. The patient size
      correction factor for males and females is body weight. Defined in Sugawara et
      al. Reevaluation of the Standardized Uptake Value for FDG: Variations with
      Body Weight and Methods for Correction.Radiology, 1999 at
      http://radiology.rsna.org/content/213/2/521
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: SUVbw
      

      Standardized Uptake Value calculated using lean body mass. The patient size
      correction factor for males is 1.10 * weight - 120 * (weight/height) ^2, and
      for females is 1.07 * weight - 148 * (weight/height) ^2. Defined in Sugawara
      et al. Reevaluation of the Standardized Uptake Value for FDG: Variations with
      Body Weight and Methods for Correction.Radiology, 1999 at
      http://radiology.rsna.org/content/213/2/521
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: SUVlbm
      

      Standardized Uptake Value calculated using body surface area. The patient size
      correction factor for males and females is weight^ 0.425 * height^0.725 *
      0.007184. Defined in Sugawara et al. Reevaluation of the Standardized Uptake
      Value for FDG: Variations with Body Weight and Methods for
      Correction.Radiology, 1999 at http://radiology.rsna.org/content/213/2/521
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: SUVbsa
      

      Standardized Uptake Value calculated using ideal body weight. The patient size
      correction factor for males is 48.0 + 1.06 * (height - 152) and for females is
      45.5 + 0.91 * (height - 152). Defined in Sugawara et al. Reevaluation of the
      Standardized Uptake Value for FDG: Variations with Body Weight and Methods for
      Correction.Radiology, 1999 at http://radiology.rsna.org/content/213/2/521
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: SUVibw
      

      Method of calculating Standardized Uptake Value using body weight. The patient
      size correction factor for males and females is body weight. Defined in
      Sugawara et al. Reevaluation of the Standardized Uptake Value for FDG:
      Variations with Body Weight and Methods for Correction.Radiology, 1999 at
      http://radiology.rsna.org/content/213/2/521
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: SUVBodyWeightCalculationMethod
      

      Method of calculating Standardized Uptake Value using lean body mass. The
      patient size correction factor for males is 1.10 * weight - 120 *
      (weight/height) ^2, and for females is 1.07 * weight - 148 * (weight/height)
      ^2. Defined in Sugawara et al. Reevaluation of the Standardized Uptake Value
      for FDG: Variations with Body Weight and Methods for Correction.Radiology,
      1999 at http://radiology.rsna.org/content/213/2/521
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: SUVLeanBodyMassCalculationMethod
      

      Method of calculating Standardized Uptake Value using body surface area. The
      patient size correction factor for males and females is weight^ 0.425 *
      height^0.725 * 0.007184. Defined in Sugawara et al. Reevaluation of the
      Standardized Uptake Value for FDG: Variations with Body Weight and Methods for
      Correction.Radiology, 1999 at http://radiology.rsna.org/content/213/2/521
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: SUVBodySurfaceAreaCalculationMethod
      

      Method of calculating Standardized Uptake Value using ideal body weight. The
      patient size correction factor for males is 48.0 + 1.06 * (height - 152) and
      for females is 45.5 + 0.91 * (height - 152). Defined in Sugawara et al.
      Reevaluation of the Standardized Uptake Value for FDG: Variations with Body
      Weight and Methods for Correction.Radiology, 1999 at
      http://radiology.rsna.org/content/213/2/521
      From: http://dicom.nema.org/resources/ontology/DCM in valuesets.xml


   .. py:attribute:: SUVIdealBodyWeightCalculationMethod
